Does he fly , then ? ''

In an Indian Jungle the season slide one into the other almost without division .
There seem to be only two -- the wet and the dry ; but if you look closely below the torrent of rain and the cloud of char and dust you will find all four go round in their regular ring .
Spring be the most wonderful , because she have not to cover a clean , bare field with new leaf and flower , but to drive before her and to put away the hanging-on , over-surviving raffle of half-green thing which the gentle winter have suffer to live , and to make the partly-dressed stale earth feel new and young once more .
And this she do so well that there be no spring in the world like the Jungle spring .
There be one day when all thing be tire , and the very smell , a they drift on the heavy air , be old and use .
One can not explain this , but it feel so .
Then there be another day -- to the eye nothing whatever have change -- when all the smell be new and delightful , and the whisker of the Jungle People quiver to their root , and the winter hair come away from their side in long , draggle lock .
Then , perhaps , a little rain fall , and all the tree and the bush and the bamboo and the moss and the juicy-leaved plant wake with a noise of grow that you can almost hear , and under this noise run , day and night , a deep hum .
THAT be the noise of the spring -- a vibrating boom which be neither bee , nor fall water , nor the wind in tree-tops , but the purring of the warm , happy world .
Up to this year Mowgli have always delight in the turn of the season .
It be he who generally saw the first Eye-of-the-Spring deep down among the grass , and the first bank of spring cloud , which be like nothing else in the Jungle .
His voice could be hear in all sort of wet , star-lighted , blossoming place , help the big frog through their chorus , or mock the little upside-down owl that hoot through the white night .
Like all his people , spring be the season he choose for his flittings -- move , for the mere joy of rush through the warm air , thirty , forty , or fifty mile between twilight and the morning star , and come back pant and laugh and wreathe with strange flower .
The Four do not follow him on these wild ringing of the Jungle , but go off to sing song with other wolf .
The Jungle People be very busy in the spring , and Mowgli could hear them grunt and scream and whistle accord to their kind .
Their voice then be different from their voice at other time of the year , and that be one of the reason why spring in the Jungle be call the Time of New Talk .
But that spring , a he tell Bagheera , his stomach be change in him .
Ever since the bamboo shoot turn spotty-brown he have be look forward to the morning when the smell should change .
But when the morning come , and Mor the Peacock , blaze in bronze and blue and gold , cry it aloud all along the misty wood , and Mowgli open his mouth to send on the cry , the word choke between his teeth , and a feeling come over him that begin at his toe and end in his hair -- a feeling of pure unhappiness , so that he look himself over to be sure that he have not tread on a thorn .
Mor cry the new smell , the other bird take it over , and from the rock by the Waingunga he hear Bagheera 's hoarse scream -- something between the scream of an eagle and the neighing of a horse .
There be a yelling and scattering of Bandar-log in the new-budding branch above , and there stand Mowgli , his chest , fill to answer Mor , sink in little gasp a the breath be drive out of it by this unhappiness .
He star all round him , but he could see no more than the mock Bandar-log scud through the tree , and Mor , his tail spread in full splendour , dance on the slope below .
`` The smell have change , '' scream Mor .
`` Good hunting , Little Brother !
Where be thy answer ? ''
`` Little Brother , good hunting ! ''
whistle Chil the Kite and his mate , swoop down together .
The two baffed under Mowgli 's nose so close that a pinch of downy white feather brush away .
A light spring rain -- elephant-rain they call it -- drive across the Jungle in a belt half a mile wide , leave the new leaf wet and nod behind , and die out in a double rainbow and a light roll of thunder .
The spring hum break out for a minute , and be silent , but all the Jungle Folk seem to be give tongue at once .
All except Mowgli .
`` I have eat good food , '' he say to himself .
`` I have drink good water .
Nor do my throat burn and grow small , a it do when I bite the blue-spotted root that Oo the Turtle say be clean food .
But my stomach be heavy , and I have give very bad talk to Bagheera and others , people of the Jungle and my people .
Now , too , I be hot and now I be cold , and now I be neither hot nor cold , but angry with that which I can not see .
Huhu !
It be time to make a running !
To-night I will cross the range ; yes , I will make a spring run to the Marshes of the North , and back again .
I have hunt too easily too long .
The Four shall come with me , for they grow as fat a white grub . ''
He call , but never one of the Four answer .
They be far beyond earshot , sing over the spring song -- the Moon and Sambhur Songs -- with the wolf of the pack ; for in the spring-time the Jungle People make very little difference between the day and the night .
He give the sharp , barking note , but his only answer be the mock maiou of the little spotted tree-cat winding in and out among the branch for early bird ' nest .
At this he shake all over with rage , and half draw his knife .
Then he become very haughty , though there be no one to see him , and stalk severely down the hillside , chin up and eyebrows down .
But never a single one of his people ask him a question , for they be all too busy with their own affair .
`` Yes , '' say Mowgli to himself , though in his heart he know that he have no reason .
`` Let the Red Dhole come from the Dekkan , or the Red Flower dance among the bamboo , and all the Jungle run whine to Mowgli , call him great elephant-names .

be I the Master of the Jungle , or be I not ?

A couple of young wolf of the Pack be canter down a path , look for open ground in which to fight .
-LRB- You will remember that the Law of the Jungle forbids fight where the Pack can see . -RRB-
Their neck-bristles be as stiff a wire , and they bay furiously , crouch for the first grapple .
Mowgli leap forward , catch one outstretched throat in either hand , expect to fling the creature backward a he have often do in game or Pack hunt .
But he have never before interfere with a spring fight .

It be a perfect white night , a they call it .

The moss curl deep and warm over his foot , the young grass have no cutting edge , and all the voice of the Jungle boom like one deep harp-string touch by the moon -- the Moon of New Talk , who splash her light full on rock and pool , slip it between trunk and creeper , and sift it through a million leaf .
Forgetting his unhappiness , Mowgli sing aloud with pure delight a he settle into his stride .
It be more like fly than anything else , for he have choose the long downward slope that lead to the Northern Marshes through the heart of the main Jungle , where the springy ground deaden the fall of his foot .
A man-taught man would have pick his way with many stumble through the cheating moonlight , but Mowgli 's muscle , train by year of experience , bore him up a though he be a feather .
When a rotten log or a hidden stone turn under his foot he save himself , never check his pace , without effort and without thought .
When he tire of ground-going he throw up his hand monkey-fashion to the near creeper , and seem to float rather than to climb up into the thin branch , whence he would follow a tree-road till his mood change , and he shot downward in a long , leafy curve to the level again .
There be still , hot hollow surround by wet rock where he could hardly breathe for the heavy scent of the night flower and the bloom along the creeper bud ; dark avenues where the moonlight lay in belt as regular a checkered marble in a church aisle ; thicket where the wet young growth stand breast-high about him and throw it arm round his waist ; and hilltop crown with broken rock , where he leap from stone to stone above the lair of the frightened little fox .
He would hear , very faint and far off , the chug-drug of a boar sharpen his tusk on a bole ; and would come across the great gray brute all alone , scribe and rend the bark of a tall tree , his mouth drip with foam , and his eye blaze like fire .
Or he would turn aside to the sound of clash horn and hiss grunt , and dash past a couple of furious sambhur , stagger to and fro with lowered head , strip with blood that show black in the moonlight .
Or at some rush ford he would hear Jacala the Crocodile bellowing like a bull , or disturb a twined knot of the Poison People , but before they could strike he would be away and across the glistening shingle , and deep in the Jungle again .
So he run , sometimes shout , sometimes sing to himself , the happy thing in all the Jungle that night , till the smell of the flower warn him that he be near the marsh , and those lay far beyond his farthest hunting-grounds .
Here , again , a man-trained man would have sink overhead in three stride , but Mowgli 's foot have eye in them , and they pass him from tussock to tussock and clump to quake clump without ask help from the eye in his head .

Mowgli whisper .

`` Ay , but again ? ''
`` Have I not follow thee to-night ? ''
`` Ay , but again and again , and it may be again , Gray Brother ? ''

`` Man go to Man at the last .

Thou , and not I -- I follow my own people -- didst let in the Jungle upon them .

They be talk a they run .

`` That be well think .

`` Hast thou , then , forget nothing ? ''
snapped Gray Brother over his shoulder , a he lay himself down to gallop , and Mowgli follow , think .

Come to the Council Rock . ''

Run and sing with u , Gray Brother . ''

`` Eee -- Yoawa ?

they would reply .

We be of one blood , thou and I -- man and snake together . ''

the boy moan .
`` My strength be go from me , and it be not any poison .

say Baloo slowly , turn his head to where Mowgli lay .

Bagheera -- where be Bagheera this night ?
-- he know also .
It be the Law . ''

It be the Law . ''

For the rest , my word be Baloo 's word . ''
He lick Mowgli 's foot .

Remember , Bagheera love thee . ''

`` There be no more .

O wise Little Frog , come to me ! ''

`` Where shall we lair to-day ?
for from now , we follow new trail . ''

CHAPTER I : Blacky The Crow Makes A Discovery Blacky the Crow be always watch for thing not intend for his sharp eye .
The result be that he get into no end of trouble which he could avoid .
In this respect he be just like his cousin , Sammy Jay .
Between them they see a great deal with which they have no business and which it would be good for them not to see .
Now Blacky the Crow find it no easy matter to pick up a living when snow cover the Green Meadows and the Green Forest , and ice bind the Big River and the Smiling Pool .
He have to use his sharp eye for all they be worth in order to find enough to fill his stomach , and he will eat anything in the way of food that he can swallow .
Often he travel long distance look for food , but at night he always come back to the same place in the Green Forest , to sleep in company with others of his family .
Blacky dearly love company , particularly at night , and about the time jolly , round , red Mr. Sun be begin to think about his bed behind the Purple Hills , you will find Blacky head for a certain part of the Green Forest where he know he will have neighbor of his own kind .

You can believe just which you please , though I suspect that neither of them really know .

One day toward the very last of winter , the notion enter his black head that he would have a look in a certain lonesome corner of the Green Forest where once upon a time Redtail the Hawk have live .

He know all about that nest .
He have visit it before when Red-tail be away .
Still it might be worth another visit .
You never can tell what you may find in old house .
Now , of course , Blacky know perfectly well that Redtail be mile and mile , hundred of mile away , and so there be nothing to fear from him .

`` There could n't , there just could n't be an egg at this time of year , or in that old tumble-down nest !

He felt sure that Hooty would stay right where he be now , and he hop that Mrs. Hooty would lose her temper and leave the nest where she be sit on those two egg and join Hooty to help him try to drive away that noisy crew .
But Hooty be n't stupid .
Not a bit of it .
The minute he find out that Blacky and his friend have discover him , he think of Mrs. Hooty and the two precious egg in the old nest of Redtail the Hawk close by .
`` Mrs. Hooty must n't be disturb , '' think he .
`` That will never do at all .
I must lead these black rascal away where they wo n't discover Mrs. Hooty .
I certainly must . ''
So he spread his broad wing and blunder away among the tree a little way .
He do n't fly far because the instant he start to fly that whole noisy crew with the exception of Blacky be after him .
Because he could n't use his claw or bill while fly , they grow bold enough to pull a few feather out of his back .
So he fly only a little way to a thick hemlock-tree , where it be n't easy for the Crows to get at him , and where the light do n't hurt his eye so much .
There he rest a few minute and then do the same thing over again .
He mean to lead those bothersome Crows into the dark part of the Green Forest and there -- well , he could see good there , and it might be that one of them would be careless enough to come within reach .
No , Hooty be n't stupid .
Certainly not .
Blacky awake to that fact a he sit in the top of a tall pine-tree silently watch .

His splendid plan have fail just because stupid Hooty , who be n't stupid at all , have fly away when he ought to have sit still .
It be very provoking .
CHAPTER VII : Blacky Tries Another Plan When one plan fail , just try another ; Declare you 'll win some way or other .
People who succeed be those who do not give up because they fail the first time they try .
They be the one who , as soon a one plan fail , get busy right away and think of another plan and try that .
If the thing they be try to do be a good thing , sooner or later they succeed .
If they be try to do a wrong thing , very likely all their plan fail , a they should .
Now Blacky the Crow know all about the value of try and try .
He be n't easily discourage .

`` Caw , caw , caw , caw ! ''

`` Caw , caw , caw , caw !
Come back , everybody !

Caw , caw , caw , caw ! ''

`` Where be the nest ? ''
they scream , a they come back to where Blacky be caw and pretend to be very much excite .

I know all about that nest . ''
And he look at Blacky a if he think Blacky be play a joke on them .

Such a racket !

He have hope , a great hope , that he would get one of those egg .
CHAPTER VIII : Hooty Comes To Mrs. Hooty 's Aid No one can live just for self alone .
A lot of people think they can , but they be very much mistaken .
They be make one of the great mistake in the world .
Every teeny , weeny act , no matter what it be , affect somebody else .
That be one of Old Mother Nature 's great law .

CHAPTER IX : Blacky Thinks Of Farmer Brown 's Boy `` Such luck ! ''

CHAPTER XI : Farmer Brown 's Boy Is Tempted When you 're tempt to do wrong Is the time to prove you 're strong .

CHAPTER XII : A Tree-Top Battle As black be black and white be white , So wrong be wrong and right be right .
There be n't any half way about it .
A thing be wrong or it be right , and that be all there be to it .
But most people have hard work to see this when they want very much to do a thing that the still small voice way down inside tell them be n't right .
They try to compromise .
To compromise be to do neither one thing nor the other but a little of both .
But you ca n't do that with right and wrong .
It be a queer thing , but a half right never be as good a a whole right , while a half wrong often , very often , be as bad a a whole wrong .
Farmer Brown 's boy , up in the tree by the nest of Hooty the Owl in the lonesome corner of the Green Forest , be fight a battle .

CHAPTER XIII : Blacky Has A Change Of Heart Blacky The Crow be n't all black .
No , indeed .

CHAPTER XIV : Blacky Makes A Call Judge no one by his style of dress ; Your ignorance you thus confess .
-- Blacky the Crow .
`` Caw , caw , caw , caw . ''

True enough , '' reply Blacky , his eye twinkle .
`` But I think they might be .
I have hear a rumor that those who go south be travel early than usual this fall , so I know I might find Mr. and Mrs. Quack over here any time now .
Is it true , Mrs. Quack , that we be go to have a long , hard , cold winter ? ''
`` That be what they say up in the Far North , '' reply Mrs. Quack .
`` And it be true that Jack Frost have start down earlier than usual .
That be how it happen we be here now .
But about those hunter over by the Big River , do you suppose they will come over here ? ''
There be an anxious note in Mrs. Quack 's voice .
`` No , '' reply Blacky promptly .
`` Farmer Brown 's boy wo n't let them .
I know .
I 've be watch him and he have be watch those hunter .
As long a you stay here , you will be safe .
What a great world this would be if all those two-legged creature be like Farmer Brown 's boy . ''
`` Would n't it ! ''
cry Peter .
Then he add , `` I wish they be . ''
`` You do n't wish it half as much a I do , '' declare Mrs. Quack .
`` Yet I can remember when he use to hunt with a terrible gun and be as bad a the bad of them , '' say Blacky .
`` What change him ? ''
ask Mrs. Quack , look interested .
`` Just get really acquaint with some of the little people of the Green Forest and the Green Meadows , '' reply Blacky .
`` He find them ready to meet him more than halfway in friendship and that some of them really be his best friend . ''
`` And now he be their best friend , '' speak up Peter .
Blacky nod .
`` Right , Peter , '' say he .
`` That be why the Quacks be safe here and will be as long a they stay . ''
CHAPTER XV : Blacky Does A Little Looking About Do not take the word of others That thing be or be not so When there be a chance that you may Find out for yourself and know .
-- Blacky the Crow .
Blacky the Crow be a shrewd fellow .
He be one of the smart and shrewd of all the little people in the Green Forest and on the Green Meadows .
Everybody know it .
And because of this , all his neighbor have a great deal of respect for him , despite his mischievous way .
Of course , Blacky have notice that Johnny Chuck have dig his house deep than usual and have stuff himself until he be fatter than ever before .
He have notice that Jerry Muskrat be make the wall of his house thicker than in other year , and that Paddy the Beaver be do the same thing to his house .
You know there be very little that escape the sharp eye of Blacky the Crow .
He have guess what these thing meant .
`` They think we be go to have a long , hard , cold winter , '' mutter Blacky to himself .
`` Perhaps they know , but I want to see some sign of it for myself .
They may be only guess .
Anybody can do that , and one guess be as good a another . ''
Then he find Mr. and Mrs. Quack , the Mallard Ducks , and their child in the pond of Paddy the Beaver and remember that they never have come down from their home in the Far North a early in the fall a this .
Mrs. Quack explain that Jack Frost have already start south , and so they have start earlier to keep well ahead of him .
`` Looks a if there may be something in this idea of a long , hard , cold winter , '' think Blacky , `` but perhaps the Quacks be only guess , too .
I would n't take their word for it any more than I would the word of Johnny Chuck or Jerry Muskrat or Paddy the Beaver .
I 'll look about a little . ''
So after warn the Quacks to remain in the pond of Paddy the Beaver if they would be safe , Blacky bid them good-by and fly away .
He head straight for the Green Meadows and Farmer Brown 's cornfield .
A little of that yellow corn would make a good breakfast .
When he reach the cornfield , Blacky perch on top of a shock of corn , for it already have be cut and put in shock in readiness to be cart up to Farmer Brown 's barn .
For a few minute he sit there silent and motionless , but all the time his sharp eye be make sure that no enemy be hide behind one of those brown shock .
When he be quite certain that thing be as safe a they seem , he pick out a plump ear of corn and begin to tear open the husk , so a to get at the yellow grain .
`` Seems to me these husk be unusually thick , '' mutter Blacky , a he tear at them with his stout bill .
`` Do n't remember ever have see them as thick a these .
Wonder if it just happen to be so on this ear . ''
Then , a a sudden thought pop into his black head , he leave that ear and go to another .
The husk of this be as thick a those on the first .
He fly to another shock and find the husk there just the same .
He try a third shock with the same result .
`` Huh , they be all alike , '' say he .
Then he look thoughtful and for a few minute sit perfectly still like a black statue .
`` They be right , '' say he at last .
`` Yes , Sir , they be right . ''
Of course he mean Johnny Chuck and Jerry Muskrat and Paddy the Beaver and the Quacks .
`` I do n't know how they know it , but they be right ; we be go to have a long , hard , cold winter .
I know it myself now .
I 've find a sign .
Old Mother Nature have wrap this corn in extra thick husk , and of course she have do it to protect it .
She do n't do thing without a reason .
We be go to have a cold winter , or my name be n't Blacky the Crow . ''
CHAPTER XVI : Blacky Finds Other Signs A single fact may fail to prove you either right or wrong ; Confirm it with another and your proof will then be strong .
-- Blacky the Crow .
After his discovery that Old Mother Nature have wrap all the ear of corn in extra thick husk , Blacky have no doubt in his own mind that Johnny Chuck and Jerry Muskrat and Paddy the Beaver and the Quacks be quite right in feel that the come winter would be long , hard and cold .
But Blacky long ago learn that it be n't wise or wholly safe to depend altogether on one thing .
`` Old Mother Nature never do thing by half , '' think Blacky , a he sit on the fence post on the Green Meadows , think over his discovery of the thick husk on the corn .
`` She would n't take care to protect the corn that way and not do as much for other thing .
There must be other sign , if I be smart enough to find them . ''
He lift one black wing and begin to set in order the feather beneath it .
Suddenly he make a funny little hop straight up .
`` Well , I never ! ''
he exclaim , a he spread his wing to regain his balance .
`` I never do ! ''
`` Is that so ? ''
pip a squeaky little voice .
`` If you say you never do , I suppose you never do , though I want the word of some one else before I will believe it .
What be it you never do ? ''
Blacky look down .
Peeping up at him from the brown grass be two bright little eye .
`` Hello , Danny Meadow Mouse ! ''
exclaim Blacky .
`` I have n't see you for a long time .
I 've look for you several time lately . ''
`` I do n't doubt it .
I do n't doubt it at all , '' squeak Danny .
`` You 'll never see me when you be look for me .
That be , you wo n't if I can help it .
You wo n't if I see you first . ''
Blacky chuckle .
He know what Danny meant .
When Blacky go look for Danny Meadow Mouse , it usually be in hope of have a Meadow Mouse dinner , and he know that Danny know this .
`` I 've have my breakfast , '' say Blacky , `` and it be n't dinner time yet . ''
`` What be it you never do ? ''
persist Danny , in his squeaky voice .
`` That be just an exclamation , '' explain Blacky .
`` I make a discovery that surprise me so I exclaim right out . ''
`` What be it ? ''
demand Danny .
`` It be that the feather of my coat be come in thicker than I ever know them to before .
I have n't notice it until I start to set them in order a minute ago . ''
He bury his bill in the feather of his breast .
`` Yes , sir , '' say he in a muffled voice , `` they be come in thicker than I ever know them to before .
There be a lot of down around the root of them .
I be go to have the warm coat I 've ever have . ''
`` Well , do n't think you be the only one , '' retort Danny .
`` My fur never be so thick at this time of year a it be now , and it be the same way with Nanny Meadow Mouse and all our child .
I suppose you know what it mean . ''
`` What do it mean ? ''
ask Blacky , just a if he do n't have the least idea , although he have guess the instant he discover those extra feather .
`` It mean we be go to have a long , hard , cold winter , and Old Mother Nature be prepare u for it , '' reply Danny , quite a if he know all about it .
`` You 'll find that everybody who do n't go south or sleep all winter have a thicker coat than usual .
Hello !
There be old Roughleg the Hawk !
He have come extra early this year .
I think I 'll go back to warn Nanny . ''
Without another word Danny disappear in the brown grass .
Again Blacky chuckle .
`` More sign , '' say he to himself .
`` More sign .
There be n't a doubt that we be go to have a hard winter .
I wonder if I can stand it or if I 'd well go a little way south , where it will be warm . ''
CHAPTER XVII : Blacky Watches A Queer Performance This much to me be very clear : A thing not understood be queer .
-- Blacky the Crow .
Blacky the Crow may be right .
Again he may not be .
If he be right , it will account for a lot of the queer people in the world .
They be not understood , and so they be queer .
At least , that be what other people say , and never once think that perhaps they be the queer one for not understand .
But Blacky be n't like those people who be satisfy not to understand and to think other people and thing queer .
He do his best to understand .
He wait and watch and us those sharp eye of his and those quick wit of his until at last usually he do understand .
The day of his discovery of Old Mother Nature 's sign that the come winter would be long , hard and cold , Blacky pay a visit to the Big River .
Long ago he discover that many thing be to be see on or beside the Big River , thing not to be see elsewhere .
So there be few clay in which he do not get over there .
As he draw near the Big River , he be very watchful and careful , be Blacky , for this be the season when hunter with terrible gun be abroad , and he have discover that they be likely to be hide along the Big River , hop to shoot Mr. or Mrs. Quack or some of their relative .
So he be very watchful a he draw near the Big River , for he have learn that it be dangerous to pass too near a hunter with a terrible gun .
More than once he have be shoot at .
But he have learn by these experience .
Oh , yes , Blacky have learn .
For one thing , he have learn to know a gun when he saw it .
For another thing , he have learn just how far away one of these dreadful gun could be and still hurt the one it be point at , and to always keep just a little farther away .
Also he have learn that a man or boy without a terrible gun be quite harmless , and he have learn that hunter with terrible gun be tricky and sometimes hide from those they seek to kill , so that in the dreadful hunting season it be best to look sharply before approach any place .
On this afternoon , a he draw near the Big River , he saw a man who seem to be very busy on the shore of the Big River , at a place where wild rice and rush grow for some distance out in the water , for just there it be shallow far out from the shore .
Blacky look sharply for a terrible gun .
But the man have none with him and therefore be not to be fear .
Blacky boldly draw near until he be able to see what the man be do .
Then Blacky 's eye stretch their widest and he almost caw right out with surprise .
The man be take yellow corn from a bag , a handful at a time , and throw it out in the water .
Yes , Sir , that be what he be do , scatter nice yellow corn among the rush and wild rice in the water !
`` That 's a queer performance , '' mutter Blacky , a he watch .
`` What be he throw perfectly good corn out in the water for ?
He be n't plant it , for this be n't the planting season .
Besides , it would n't grow in the water , anyway .
It be a shame to waste nice corn like that .
What be he do it for ? ''
Blacky fly over to a tree some distance away and alight in the top of it to watch the queer performance .
You know Blacky have very keen eye and he can see a long distance .
For a while the man continue to scatter corn and Blacky continue to wonder what he be do it for .
At last the man go away in a boat .
Blacky watch him until he be out of sight .
Then he spread his wing and slowly fly back and forth just above the rush and wild rice , at the place where the man have be scatter the corn .
He could see some of the yellow grain on the bottom .
Presently he saw something else .
`` Ha ! ''
exclaim Blacky .
CHAPTER XVIII : Blacky Becomes Very Suspicious Of thing you do not understand , Beware !
They may be wholly harmless but -- Beware !
You 'll find the old that you grow That only thing and folk you know Are fully to be trust , so Beware !
-- Blacky the Crow .
That be one of Blacky 's wise saying , and he live up to it .
It be one reason why he have come to be regard by all his neighbor a one of the smart of all who live in the Green Forest and on the Green Meadow .
He seldom get into any real trouble because he first make sure there be no trouble to get into .
When he discover something he do not understand , he be at once distrustful of it .
As he watch a man scatter yellow corn in the water from the shore of the Big River he at once become suspicious .
He could n't understand why a man should throw good corn among the rush and wild rice in the water , and because he could n't understand , he at once begin to suspect that it be for no good purpose .
When the man leave in a boat , Blacky slowly fly over the rush where the man have throw the corn , and presently his sharp eye make a discovery that cause him to exclaim right out .
What be it Blacky have discover ?
Only a few feather .
No one with eye less sharp than Blacky 's would have notice them .
And few would have give them a thought if they have notice them .
But Blacky know right away that those be feather from a Duck .
He know that a Duck , or perhaps a flock of Ducks , have be rest or feed in there among those rush , and that in move about they have leave those two or three downy feather .
`` Ha ! ''
exclaim Blacky .
`` Mr. and Mrs. Quack or some of their relative have be here .
It be just the kind of a place Ducks like .
Also some Ducks like corn .
If they should come back here and find this corn , they would have a feast , and they would be sure to come again .
That man who scatter the corn here do n't have a terrible gun , but that do n't mean that he be n't a hunter .
He may come back again , and then he may have a terrible gun .
I 'm suspicious of that man .
I be so .
I believe he put that corn here for Ducks and I do n't believe he do it out of the kindness of his heart .
If it be Farmer Brown 's boy I would know that all be well ; that he be think of hungry Ducks , with few place where they can fee in safety , a they make the long journey from the Far North to the Sunny South .
But it be n't Farmer Brown 's boy .
I do n't like the look of it .
I do n't indeed .
I 'll keep watch of this place and see what happen . ''
All the way to his favorite perch in a certain big hemlock-tree in the Green Forest , Blacky keep think about that corn and the man who have seem to be generous with it , and the more he think , the more suspicious he become .
He do n't like the look of it at all .
`` I 'll warn the Quacks to keep away from there .
I 'll do it the very first thing in the morning , '' he mutter , a he prepare to go to sleep .
`` If they have any sense at all , they will stay in the pond of Paddy the Beaver .
But if they should go over to the Big River , they would be almost sure to find that corn , and if they should once find it , they would keep go back for more .
It may be all right , but I do n't like the look of it . ''
And still full of suspicion , Blacky go to sleep .
CHAPTER XIX : Blacky Makes More Discoveries Little thing you fail to see May important prove to be .
-- Blacky the Crow .
One of the secret of Blacky 's success in life be the fact that he never fail to take note of little thing .
Long ago he learn that little thing which in themselves seem harmless and not worth notice may together prove the most important thing in life .
So , no matter how unimportant a thing may appear , Blacky examine it closely with those sharp eye of his and remembers it .
The very first thing Blacky do , as soon a he be awake the morning after he discover the man scatter corn in the rush at a certain place on the edge of the Big River , be to fly over to the pond of Paddy the Beaver and again warn Mr. and Mrs. Quack to keep away from the Big River , if they and their six child would remain safe .
Then he get some breakfast .
He eat it in a hurry and fly straight over to the Big River to the place where he have see that yellow corn scatter .
Blacky be n't wholly surprise to find Dusky the Black Duck , own cousin to Mr. and Mrs. Quack the Mallard Ducks , with a number of his relative in among the rush and wild rice at the very place where that corn have be scatter .
They seem quite contented and in the best of spirit .
Blacky guess why .
Not a single grain of that yellow corn could Blacky see .
He know the way of Dusky and his relative .
He know that they must have come in there just at dusk the night before and at once have find that corn .
He know that they would remain hide there until frighten out , and that then they would spend the day in some little pond where they would not be likely to be disturb or where at least no danger could approach them without be see in plenty of time .
There they would rest all day , and when the Black Shadows come creep out from the Purple Hills , they would return to that place on the Big River to fee , for that be the time when they like best to hunt for their food .
Dusky look up a Blacky fly over him , but Blacky say nothing , and Dusky say nothing .
But if Blacky do n't use his tongue , he do use his eye .
He saw just on the edge of the shore what look like a lot of small bush grow close together on the very edge of the water .
Mixed in with them be a lot of the brown rush .
They look very harmless and innocent .
But Blacky know every foot of that shore along the Big River , and he know that those bush have n't be there during the summer .
He know that they have n't grow there .
He fly directly over them .
Just back of them be a couple of log .
Those log have n't be there when he pass that way a few day before .
He be sure of it .
`` Ha ! ''
exclaim Blacky under his breath .
`` Those look to me a if they might be very handy , very handy indeed , for a hunter to sit on .
Sitting there behind those bush , he would be hide from any Duck who might come in to look for nice yellow corn scatter out there among the rush .
It do n't look right to me .
No , Sir , it do n't look right to me .
I think I 'll keep an eye on this place . ''
So Blacky come back to the Big River several time that day .
The second time back he find that Dusky the Black Duck and his relative have leave .
When he return in the afternoon , he saw the same man he have see there the afternoon before , and he be do the same thing , -- scatter yellow corn out in the rush .
And a before , he go away in a boat .
`` I do n't like it , '' mutter Blacky , shake his black head .
`` I do n't like it . ''
CHAPTER XX : Blacky Drops A Hint When you see another 's danger Warn him though he be a stranger .
-- Blacky the Crow .
Every day for a week a man come in a boat to scatter corn in the rush at a certain point along the bank of the Big River , and every day Blacky the Crow watch him and shake his black head and talk to himself and tell himself that he do n't like it , and that he be sure that it be for no good purpose .
Sometimes Blacky watch from a distance , and sometimes he fly right over the man .
But never once do the man have a gun with him .
Every morning , very early , Blacky fly over there , and every morning he find Dusky the Black Duck and his flock in the rush and wild rice at that particular place , and he know that they have be there all night , He know that they have come in there just at dusk the night before , to feast on the yellow corn the man have scatter there in the afternoon .
`` It be no business of mine what those Ducks do , '' mutter Blacky to himself , `` but as surely a my tail feather be black , something be go to happen to some of them one of these day .
That man may be fool them , but he be n't fool me .
Not a bit of it .
He have n't have a gun with him once when I have see him , but just the same he be a hunter .
I feel it in my bone .
He know those silly Ducks come in here every night for that corn he put out .
He know that after they have be here a few time and nothing have frighten them , they will be so sure that it be a safe place that they will not be the least bit suspicious .
Then he will hide behind those bush he have place close to the edge of the water and wait for them with his terrible gun .
That be what he will do , or my name be n't Blacky . ''
Finally Blacky decide to drop a hint to Dusky the Black Duck .
So the next morning he stop for a call .
`` Good morning , '' say he , a Dusky swam in just in front of him .
`` I hope you be feel as fine a you look . ''
`` Quack , quack , '' reply Dusky .
`` When Blacky the Crow flatters , he hop to gain something .
What be it this time ? ''
`` Not a thing , '' reply Blacky .
`` On my honor , not a thing .
There be nothing for me here , though there seem to be plenty for you and your relative , to judge by the fact that I find you in this same place every morning .
What be it ? ''
`` Corn , '' reply Dusky in a low voice , a if afraid some one might overhear him .
`` Nice yellow corn . ''
`` Corn ! ''
exclaim Blacky , a if very much astonish .
`` How do corn happen to be way over here in the water ? ''
Dusky shake his head .
`` Do n't ask me , for I ca n't tell you , '' say he .
`` I have n't the least idea .
All I know be that every evening when we arrive , we find it here .
How it get here , I do n't know , and furthermore I do n't care .
It be enough for me that it be here . ''
`` I 've see a man over here every afternoon , '' say Blacky .
`` I think he might be a hunter . ''
`` Did he have a terrible gun ? ''
ask Dusky suspiciously .
`` No-o , '' reply Blacky .
`` Then he be n't a hunter , '' declare Dusky , look much relieve .
`` But perhaps one of these day he will have one and will wait for you to come in for your dinner , '' suggest Blacky .
`` He could hide behind these bush , you know . ''
`` Nonsense , '' retort Dusky , toss his head .
`` There have n't be a sign of danger here since we have be here .
I know you , Blacky ; you be jealous because we find plenty to eat here , and you find nothing .
You be try to scare u .
But I 'll tell you right now , you ca n't scare u away from such splendid eating a we have have here .
So there ! ''
CHAPTER XXI : At Last Blacky Is Sure Who for another conquers fear Is truly brave , it be most clear .
-- Blacky the Crow .
It be late in the afternoon , and Blacky the Crow be on his way to the Green Forest .
As usual , he go around by the Big River to see if that man be scatter corn for the Ducks .
He be n't there .
No one be to be see along the bank of the Big River .
`` He have n't come to-day , or else he come early and have leave , '' think Blacky .
And then his sharp eye catch sight of something that make him turn aside and make straight for a certain tree , from the top of which he could see all that go on for a long distance .
What be it Blacky saw ?
It be a boat come down the Big River .
Blacky sit still and watch .
Presently the boat turn in among the rush , and a moment later a man step out on the shore .
It be the same man Blacky have watch scatter corn in the rush every day for a week .
There be n't the least doubt about it , it be the same man .
`` Ha , ha ! ''
exclaim Blacky , and nearly lose his balance in his excitement .
`` Ha , ha !
It be just a I think ! ''
You see Blacky 's sharp eye have see that the man be carry something , and that something be a gun , a terrible gun .
Blacky know a terrible gun as far a he can see it .
The hunter , for of course that be what he be , tramp along the shore until he reach the bush which Blacky have notice close to the water and which he know have not grow there .
The hunter look out over the Big River .
Then he walk along where he have scatter corn the day before .
Not a grain be to be see .
This seem to please him .
Then he go back to the bush and sit down on a log behind them , his terrible gun across his knee .
`` I be sure of it , '' mutter Blacky .
`` He be go to wait there for those Ducks to come in , and then something dreadful will happen .
What terrible creature these hunter be !
They do n't know what fairness be .
No , Sir , they do n't know what fairness be .
He have put food there day after day , where Dusky the Black Duck and his flock would be sure to find it , and have wait until they have become so sure there be no danger that they be no longer suspicious .
He know they will feel so sure that all be safe that they will come in without look for danger .
Then he will fire that terrible gun and kill them without give them any chance at all .
`` Reddy Fox be a sly , clever hunter , but he would n't do a thing like that .
Neither would Old Man Coyote or anybody else who wear fur or feather .
They might hide and try to catch some one by surprise .
That be all right , because each of u be suppose to be on the watch for thing of that sort .
Oh , dear , what 's to be do ?
It be time I be get home to the Green Forest .
The Black Shadows will soon come creep out from the Purple Hills , and I must be safe in my hemlock-tree by then .
I would be scar to death to be out after dark .
Yet those Ducks ought to be warn .
Oh , dear , what shall I do ? ''
Blacky peer over at the Green Forest and then over toward the Purple Hills , behind which jolly , round , red Mr. Sun would go to bed very shortly .
He shiver a he think of the Black Shadows that soon would come swiftly out from the Purple Hills across the Big River and over the Green Meadows .
With them might come Hooty the Owl , and Hooty would n't object in the least to a Crow dinner .
He wish he be in that hemlock-tree that very minute .
Then Blacky look at the hunter with his terrible gun and thought of what might happen , what would be almost sure to happen , unless those Ducks be warn .
`` I 'll wait a little while long , '' mutter Blacky , and try to feel brave .
But instead he shiver .
CHAPTER XXII : Blacky Goes Home Happy No great happiness be win Than through a deed for others do .
-- Blacky the Crow .
Blacky sit in the top of a tree near the bank of the Big River and could n't make up his mind what to do .
He want to get home to the big , thick hemlock-tree in the Green Forest before dusk , for Blacky be afraid of the dark .
That be , he be afraid to be out after dark .
`` Go along home , '' say a voice inside him , `` there be hardly time now for you to get there before the Black Shadows arrive .
Do n't waste any more time here .
What may happen to those silly Ducks be no business of yours , and there be nothing you can do , anyway .
Go along home . ''
`` Wait a few minute , '' say another little voice down inside him .
`` Do n't be a coward .
You ought to warn Dusky the Black Duck and his flock that a hunter with a terrible gun be wait for them .
Is it true that it be no business of yours what happen to those Ducks ?
Think again , Blacky ; think again .
It be the duty of each one who see a common danger to warn his neighbor .
If something dreadful should happen to Dusky because you be afraid of the dark , you never would be comfortable in your own mind .
Stay a little while and keep watch . ''
Not five minute later Blacky saw something that make him , oh , so glad he have keep watch .
It be a swiftly move black line just above the water far down the Big River , and it be come up .
He know what that black line be .
He look over at the hunter hiding behind some bush close to the edge of the water .
The hunter be crouch with his terrible gun in his hand and be peep over the bush , watch that black line .
He , too , know what it be .
It be a flock of Ducks fly .
Blacky be all ashake again , but this time it be n't with fear of be catch away from home in the dark ; it be with excitement .
He know that those Ducks have become so eager for more of that corn , that delicious yellow corn which every night for a week they have find scatter in the rush just in front of the place where that hunter be now hide , that they could n't wait for the come of the Black Shadows .
They be so sure there be no danger that they be come in to eat without wait for the Black Shadows , a they usually do .
And Blacky be glad .
Perhaps now he could give them warn .
Up the middle of the Big River , fly just above the water , sweep the flock with Dusky at it head .
How swiftly they fly , those nine big bird !
Blacky envy them their swift wing .
On past the hidden hunter but far out over the Big River they sweep .
For just a minute Blacky think they be go on up the river and not come in to eat , after all .
Then they turn toward the other shore , sweep around in a circle and head straight in toward that hidden hunter .
Blacky glance at him and saw that he be ready to shoot .
Almost without thinking , Blacky spread his wing and start out from that tree .
`` Caw , caw , caw , caw , caw ! ''
he shriek at the top of his lung .
`` Caw , caw , caw , caw , caw ! ''
It be his danger cry that everybody on the Green Meadows and in the Green Forest know .
Instantly Dusky turn and begin to climb up , up , up , the other Ducks follow him until , a they pass over the hidden hunter , they be so high it be useless for him to shoot .
He do put up his gun and aim at them , but he do n't shoot .
You see , he do n't want to frighten them so that they would not return .
Then the flock turn and start off in the direction from which they have come , and in a few minute they be merely a black line disappear far down the Big River .
Blacky head straight for the Green Forest , chuckle a he fly .
He know that those Ducks would not return until after dark .
He have save them this time , and he be so happy he do n't even notice the Black Shadows .

CHAPTER XXIII : Blacky Calls Farmer Brown 's Boy Blacky awoke in the best of spirit .

CHAPTER XXIV : Farmer Brown 's Boy Does Some Thinking Farmer Brown 's boy sit on the bank of the Big River in a brown study .

He have just as much right here a I have .

CHAPTER XXV : Blacky Gets A Dreadful Shock When friend prove false , whom may we trust ?
The spring of faith be turn to dust .
-- Blacky the Crow .
Blacky the Crow be in the top of his favorite tree over near the Big River early this afternoon .

CHAPTER XXVI : Why The Hunter Got No Ducks The hunter who have come down the Big River in a boat and land near the place where Dusky the Black Duck and his flock have find nice yellow corn scatter in the rush night after night saw Blacky the Crow leave the top of a certain tree a he approach .

CHAPTER XXVII : The Hunter Gives Up Blacky The Crow do n't know what to think .

CHAPTER XXVIII : Blacky Has A Talk With Dusky The Black Duck Doubt not a friend , but to the last Grip hard on faith and hold it fast .
-- Blacky the Crow .

CHAPTER XXIX : Blacky Discovers An Egg Blacky be fond of egg , a you know .
In this he be a great deal like other people , Farmer Brown 's boy for instance .
But a Blacky can not keep hen , a Farmer Brown 's boy do , he be oblige to steal egg or else go without .
If you come right down to plain , everyday truth , I suppose Blacky be n't so far wrong when he insist that he be no more of a thief than Farmer Brown 's boy .
Blacky say that the egg which the ben lay belong to the hen , and that he , Blacky have just as much right to take them a Farmer Brown 's boy .
He quite overlook the fact that Farmer Brown 's boy feed the biddy and take the egg a pay .
Anyway , that be what Farmer Brown 's boy say , but I do not know whether or not the biddy understand it that way .
So Blacky the Crow can not see why he should not help himself to an egg when he get the chance .
He do n't get the chance very often to steal egg from the hen , because usually they lay their egg in the henhouse , and Blacky be too suspicious to venture inside .
The egg he do get be mostly those of his neighbor in the Green Forest and the Old Orchard .
But once in a great while some foolish hen will make a nest outside the henhouse somewhere , and if Blacky happen to find it the black scamp watch every minute he can spare from other mischief for a chance to steal an egg .
Now Blacky know just what a rogue Farmer Brown 's boy think he be , and for this reason Blacky be very careful about approach Farmer Brown or any other man until he have make sure that he run no risk of be shot .

He also know that without a terrible gun , there be little Farmer Brown or any one else can do to him .
So when he see Farmer Brown out in his field , Blacky often will fly right over him and shout `` Caw , caw , caw , ca-a-w ! ''
in the most provoking way , and Fanner Brown 's boy insist that he have see Blacky wink when he be do it .

You see , he have learn that there be door and window in building , and out of one of these a terrible gun may bang at any time .

First he sit in a tall tree from which he can watch Farmer Brown 's home .

If he be quite sure that no one be about , he sometimes drop down into the henyard and help himself to corn , if any happen to be there .

It be a box just inside the henhouse door .

In fact , he be sure that he saw two egg there .

She do n't seem frighten , but very proud .

He be afraid that it would bring some one to find out what be go on .

You see , a he rise into the air , he manage to pass that open door in such a way that he could glance in .
That one glance be enough .
You know Blacky 's eye be very sharp .
He saw the hay in the box and the two egg in the hay , and that be enough for him .
From that instant Blacky the Crow begin to scheme and plan to get one or both of those egg .
It seem to him that he never , never , have want anything quite so much , and he be sure that he would not and could not be happy until he succeed in get one .
CHAPTER XXX : Blacky Screws Up His Courage If out of sight , then out of mind .
This be a say which you often hear .
It may be true sometimes , but it be very far from true at other time .
Take the case of Blacky .
He have have only a glance into that nest just inside the door of Farmer Brown 's henhouse , but that glance have be enough to show him two egg there .
Then , a he fly away toward the Green Forest , those egg be out of sight , of course .
But do you think they be out of mind ?
Not much !
No , indeed !
In fact , those egg be very much in Blacky 's mind .
He could n't think of anything else .
He fly straight to a certain tall pine-tree in a lonely part of the Green Forest .
Whenever Blacky want to think or to plan mischief , he seek that particular tree , and in the shelter of it broad branch he keep out of sight of curious eye , and there he sit as still a still can be .

I do n't like have to go inside that henhouse , even though it be barely inside the door .
I 'm suspicious of door .
They have a way of close most unexpectedly .
I might see if I can not get Unc ' Billy Possum to bring one of those egg out for me .
But that plan wo n't do , come to think of it , because I ca n't trust Unc ' Billy .
The old sinner be too fond of egg himself .
I would be willing to divide with him , but he would be sure to eat his first , and I fear that it would taste so good that he would eat the other .
No .
I 've get to get one of those egg myself .
It be the only way I can be sure of it .
`` The thing to do be to make sure that Farmer Brown 's boy and Farmer Brown himself be nowhere about .
They ought to be down in the cornfield pretty soon .
With them down there , I have only to watch my chance and slip in .
It wo n't take but a second .
Just a little courage , Blacky , just a little courage !
Nothing in this world worth have be gain without some risk .
The thing to do be to make sure that the risk be as small a possible . ''
Blacky shake out his feather and then fly out of the tall pine-tree as silently a he have fly into it .
He head straight toward Farmer Brown 's cornfield .
When he be near enough to see all over the field , he drop down to the top of a fence post , and there he wait .
He do n't have long to wait .
In fact , he have be there but a few minute when he spy two people come down the Long Lane toward the cornfield .
He look at them sharply , and then give a little sigh of satisfaction .
They be Farmer Brown and Farmer Brown 's boy .
Presently they reach the cornfield and turn into it .
Then they go to work , and Blacky know that so far a they be concern , the way be clear for him to visit the henyard .
He do n't fly straight there .
Oh , my , no !
Blacky be too clever to do anything like that .
He fly toward the Green Forest .
When he know that he be out of sight of those in the cornfield , he turn and fly over to the Old Orchard , and from the top of one of the old apple-trees he study the henyard and the barnyard and Farmer Brown 's house and the barn , to make absolutely sure that there be no danger near .
When he be quite sure , he silently fly down into the henyard a he have do many time before .
He pretend to be look for scattered grain of corn , but all the time he be edge nearer and nearer to the open door of the henhouse .
At last he could see the box with the hay in it .
He walk right up to the open door and peer inside .
There be nothing to be afraid of that he could see .
Still he hesitate .
He do hate to go inside that door , even for a minute , and that be all it would take to fly up to that nest and get one of those egg .
Blacky close his eye for just a second , and when he do that he seem to see himself eat one of those egg .
`` What be you afraid of ? ''
he mutter to himself a he open his eye .
Then with a hurried look in all direction , he fly up to the edge of the box .
There lay the two egg !
CHAPTER XXXI : An Egg That Would n't Behave If you have an egg and it would n't behave Just what would you do with that egg , may I ask ?
To make an egg do what it do n't want to do Strikes me like a difficult sort of a task .
All of which be pure nonsense .
Of course .
Who ever heard of an egg either behaving or misbehaving ?
Nobody .
That be , nobody that I know , unless it be Blacky .

Bowser the Hound .

CHAPTER XIX WHERE WAS BOWSER THE HOUND ?

In his eye be such a look of pain and suffering as would have touch the hard heart .

It seem to him that he have go a terribly long distance , though really it be not far at all , when something tickle his nose , that wonderful nose which can smell the track of others long after they have pass .
But this time it be n't the smell of a track that tickle his nose ; it be something in the air .
Bowser lift his head and sniffed long and hard .
What he smell be smoke .
He know what that meant .
Somewhere not very far ahead of him be a house .

-RSB- With new hope and courage Bowser try to hurry on .
Presently around a turn of the road he saw a farmyard .
The smell of the smoke from the chimney of the farmhouse be strong now , and with it be mingle an appetizing smell of thing cook .
Into Bowser 's whimper there now creep a little note of eagerness a he drag himself across the farmyard and up to the back door .
There his strength quite leave him .
He do n't have enough leave to even bark .
All he could do be whine .
After what seem a long , long time the door open , and a motherly woman stand look down at him .
Two minute later Bowser lay on a mat close by the kitchen stove .
CHAPTER XXI BOWSER BECOMES A PRISONER There be no one in all the Great World more faithful than a faithful dog .
Bowser the Hound .
Bowser the Hound be a prisoner .
Yes , Sir , Bowser be a sure-enough prisoner .
But there be a great difference in prison .
Bowser be a prisoner of kindness .
It seem funny that kindness should ever make any one a prisoner , but it be so sometimes .
You see , it be this way : When Bowser have be take in to that strange farmhouse , he have be so use up that he have have only strength enough to very feebly wag his tail .
Right away the people in that farmhouse know what have happen to Bowser .
That be , they know part of what have happen to him .
They know that he have be lose and have somehow hurt one leg .
They be very , very good to him .
They feed him , and make a comfortable bed for him , and rub something on the leg which he have hurt and which have swell .
Almost right away after eat Bowser go to sleep and sleep and sleep and sleep .
It be the very best thing he could have do .
The next day he felt a whole lot well , but he be so stiff and lame that he could hardly move .
He do n't try very much .
He be pet and care for quite as tenderly a he would have be at his own home .
So several day pass , and Bowser be begin to feel more like himself .
The more he felt like himself , the more he want to go home .
It be n't that there he would receive any great kindness than he be now receive , but home be home and there be no place like it .
So Bowser begin to be uneasy .
`` This dog do n't belong anywhere around here , '' say the man of the house .
`` I know every Hound for mile around , and I never have see this one before .
He have come a long distance .
It will not do to let him go , for he will try to find his way home and the chance be that he will again get lose .
We must keep him in the house or chain up .
Perhaps some day we may be able to find his owner .
If not , we will keep him .
I be sure he will soon become content here . ''
Now that man know dog .
Had Bowser have the chance , he would have do exactly what that man have say .
He would have try to find his way home , and he have n't the least idea in the world in which direction home lay .
But he do n't get the chance to try .
When he be allow to run out of door it be always with some one to watch him .
He be pet and baby and make a great deal of , but he know all the time that he be a prisoner .
He know that if he be to get away at all he would have to sneak away , and somehow there never seem a chance to do this .
He be grateful to these kindly people , but down in his heart be a great longing for Farmer Brown 's boy and home .
He always felt this longing just a wee bit strong when Blacky the Crow pass over and caw .
CHAPTER XXII FARMER BROWN 'S BOY LOOKS IN VAIN Loyalty be priceless and Is neither sell nor buy .
Alas , how few who seem to know Its value a they ought .
Bowser the Hound .
As I have tell you , Farmer Brown 's boy have be all about the neighborhood ask at each farmhouse if anything have be see of Bowser .
Of course nothing have be see of him , and so at last Farmer Brown 's boy felt sure that something dreadful have happen to Bowser in the wood .
For several day he tramp through the Green Forest and up through the Old Pasture , look for sign of Bowser .
His heart be heavy , for you know Bowser be quite one of the family .
He visit every place he could think of where he and Bowser have hunt together .
He know that by this time Bowser could n't possibly be alive if he have be catch by a foot in a trap or have meet with an accident in the wood .
He have quite give up all hope of ever see Bowser alive again .
But he do want to know just what have happen to him , and so he keep search and search .
One day Farmer Brown 's boy heard that a strange dog have be find over in the next township .
That afternoon he drive over there , his heart fill with great hope .
But he have his long ride for nothing , for when he get there he find that the strange dog be not Bowser at all .
Meanwhile Old Man Coyote and Reddy Fox and Old Granny Fox have become very bold .
They even come up around the henyard in broad daylight .
`` I believe you know something about what have become of Bowser , '' Farmer Brown 's boy say , a he chase Old Man Coyote away one day .
`` You certainly know that he be n't home , and I more than suspect that you know why he be n't home .
I certainly shall have to get another dog to teach you not to be so bold . ''
But somehow Farmer Brown 's boy could n't bring himself quite to take such a step a get a new dog .
He felt that no other dog ever could take Bowser 's place , and in spite of the fact that he think he have give up all hope of ever see Bowser again , ` way down deep inside be something which , if it be not hope , be something enough like it to keep him from get another dog in Bowser 's place .
Whenever he go about away from home , he keep an eye out for dog in the farmyard he pass .
He do it without really think anything about it .
He have give up hope of find Bowser , yet he be always look for him .
CHAPTER XXIII BOWSER 'S GREAT VOICE To long for home when far away Will rob of joy the bright day .
Bowser the Hound .
There be as much difference in the voice of dog a in the voice of human being .
For that matter , this be true of many of the little people who wear fur .
Bowser the Hound have a wonderful , deep , clear voice , a voice that could be hear a great distance .
No one who know it would ever mistake it for the voice of any other Hound .
As a rule , Bowser seldom use that great voice of his save when he be hunt some one .
Then , when the scent be strong , he give tongue so fast that you wonder how he have breath enough leave to run .
But now that he be a prisoner of kindness , in the home of the people who have take him in when he have creep to their doorstep , Bowser sometimes bay from sheer homesickness .
When he be tie out in the yard , he would sometimes get to think of his home and long to see Farmer Brown and Mrs. Brown and especially his master , Farmer Brown 's boy .
Then , when he could stand it no longer , he would open his mouth and send his great voice roll across to the wood with a tone of mournfulness which never have be there before .
But great a be Bowser 's voice , and far a it would carry , there be none who know him to hear it , save Blacky the Crow .
You remember that Blacky know just where Bowser be and often fly over that farmyard to make sure that Bowser be still there .
So more than once Blacky hear Bowser 's great voice with it mournful note , and understand it .
It trouble Blacky .
Yes , Sir , it actually trouble Blacky .
He know just what be the matter with Bowser , but for the life of him he could n't think of any way of help Bowser .
`` That dog be homesick , '' croak Blacky , a he sit in the top of a tall tree , scratch his head a if he think he might scratch an idea out of it .
`` Of course he do n't know how to get home , and if he try he probably would get a badly lose a he be before .
Anyway , they do n't give him a chance to try .
I ca n't lead Farmer Brown 's boy over here because he do n't understand my talk , and I do n't understand his .
There be n't a thing I can do but keep watch .
I wish Bowser would stop barking .
It make me feel uncomfortable .
Yes , Sir , it make me feel uncomfortable .
Old Man Coyote get Bowser into this trouble , and he ought to get him out again , but I do n't suppose it be the least bit of use to ask him .
It wo n't do any harm to try , anyway . ''
So Blacky start back for the Green Forest and the Old Pasture near Farmer Brown 's to look for Old Man Coyote , and for a long time a he fly he could hear Bowser 's voice with it note of homesickness and longing .
CHAPTER XXIV BLACKY TRIES TO GET HELP You 'll find that nothing more worth while can be Than help others whose distress you see .
Bowser the Hound .
On his way back to the Green Forest near Farmer Brown 's home , Blacky the Crow keep a sharp watch for Old Man Coyote .
But Old Man Coyote be nowhere to be see , and it be too late to go look for him , because jolly , round , red Mr. Sun have already go to bed behind the Purple Hills and the Black Shadows be hurry towards the Green Forest .
Blacky never be out after dark .
You might think that one with so black a coat would be fond of the Black Shadows , but it be n't so at all .
The fact be , bold and impudent a Blacky the Crow be in daylight , he be afraid of the dark .
He be quite as timid a anybody I know of in the dark .
So Blacky always contrive to go to bed early and be securely hidden away in his secret roosting-place by the time the Black Shadows reach the edge of the Green Forest .
Perhaps it be n't quite fair to say that Blacky be afraid of the dark .
It be n't the dark itself that Blacky fear , but it be one who be abroad in the dark .
It be Hooty the Owl .
Hooty would just as soon dine on Blacky the Crow a he would on any one else , and Blacky know it .
The next morning , bright and early , Blacky fly over to the Old Pasture to the home of Old Man Coyote .
Just a he get there he saw Old Man Coyote come home from an all-night hunt .
`` I hope you have have good hunting , '' say Blacky politely .
Old Man Coyote look up at Blacky sharply .
Blacky be polite only when he want to get something .
`` There be plenty of hunting , but little enough reward for it , '' reply Old Man Coyote .
`` What bring you over here so early ?
I should suppose you would be look for a breakfast . ''
Now Blacky the Crow be a very wise fellow .
He know when it be to be sly and crafty and when it be best to be frank and out-spoken .
This be a time for the latter .
`` I know where Bowser the Hound be , '' say Blacky .
`` I saw him yesterday . ''
Old Man Coyote prick up his ear and grin .
`` I think he be dead , '' say he .
`` It 's a long time since we 've hear from Bowser .
Is he well ? ''
`` Quite well , '' reply Blacky , `` but unhappy .
He be homesick .
I suspect that the trouble with Bowser be that he have n't the least idea in which direction home lie .
You enjoy run , so why not go with me to pay Bowser a visit and then lead him back home ? ''
Old Man Coyote throw back his head and laugh in that crazy fashion of his till the very hill rang with the sound of his voice .
CHAPTER XXV BLACKY CALLS ON REDDY FOX Saying what you mean , and mean what you say Are matter quite as different a night be from the day .
Bowser the Hound .
Blacky the Crow waste no time with Old Man Coyote after he hear Old Man Coyote laugh .
There be a note in that crazy laugh of Old Man Coyote 's that tell Blacky he might just as well talk to the rock or the tree about help Bowser the Hound .
Old Man Coyote have lead Bowser into his trouble , and it be quite clear that not only do he have no regret , but he be actually glad that Bowser be not likely to return .
`` You 're a hard-hearted old sinner , '' declare Blacky , a he prepare to fly in search of Reddy Fox .
Old Man Coyote grin .
`` It be every one for himself , you know , '' say he .
`` Bowser would do his best to catch me if he have the chance .
So if he be in trouble , he can stay there for all of me . ''
It do n't take Blacky long to find Reddy Fox .
You see , it be so early in the morning that Reddy have not retire for his daily nap .
Like Old Man Coyote , he be just return from a night 's hunt when Blacky arrive .
`` Hello , Reddy ! ''
exclaim Blacky .
`` You certainly be look in mighty fine condition .
That red coat of yours be the handsome coat I 've ever see .
If I have a coat like that I know I should be so swell up with pride that I just would n't be able to see common folk .
I 'm glad you 're not that way , Reddy .
One of the thing I like about you be the fact that you never allow your fine coat to make you proud .
That be more than I can say for some folk I know . ''
Reddy Fox sit down with his big bushy tail curl around to keep his toe warm , cock his head on one side , and look up at Blacky the Crow a if he be try to see right inside that black head to find out what be go on there .
`` Now what have that black scamp get in his mind , '' think Reddy .
`` He never pay compliment unless he want something in return .
That old black rascal have the smooth tongue in the Green Forest .
He have n't come ` way over here just to tell me that I have a handsome coat .
He would n't fly over a fence to tell anybody that unless it be for a purpose . ''
Aloud he say , `` Good morning , Blacky .
I suppose I must admit I have a fine coat .
Perhaps I do look very fine , but if you could see under this red coat of mine , you would find mighty little meat on my rib .
To be quite honest , I be not feel half as fine a I look .
You lucky fellow who can fly and do n't have to think about distance may be able to live well these day , but a for me , I 've forget when last I have a good meal . ''
CHAPTER XXVI RED WITS AND BLACK WITS This fact you 'll find be always so : He 's quick of wit who fool a Crow .
Bowser the Hound .
There be no great flatterer in the Green Forest or on the Green Meadows than Blacky the Crow when he hop to gain something thereby .
His tongue be so smooth that it be a wonder it do not drip oil .
He be crafty , be Blacky .
But these same thing be true of Reddy Fox .
No one ever yet have a chance to accuse Reddy Fox of lack in sharp wit .
Mistakes he make , a everybody do , but Reddy 's wit be always keen and active .
Now Reddy know perfectly well that Blacky want something of him , and this be why he be say such pleasant thing .
Blacky the Crow know that Reddy know this thing , and that if he would make use of Reddy a he hop to , he must contrive to keep Reddy wholly in the dark a to what he want do .
So a they sit there , Reddy Fox on the snow with his tail curl around his foot to keep them warm , and Blacky the Crow in the top of a little tree above Reddy 's head , they be play a sort of game .
It be red wit against black wit .
Reddy be try to outguess Blacky , and Blacky be try to outguess Reddy , and both be enjoy it .
People with sharp wit always enjoy match their wit against other sharp wit .
When Reddy Fox say that in spite of his fine appearance he have forget when last he have have a good meal , Blacky pretend to think he be joke .
`` You surprise me , '' say he .
`` Whatever be the matter with my good friend Reddy , that he go hungry when he no longer have anything to fear from Bowser the Hound .
By the way , I saw Bowser the other day . ''
At this , just for an instant , Reddy 's eye fly wide open .
Then they half close again until they be just two yellow slit .
But quickly a he close them , Blacky have see that startled surprise .
`` Yes , '' say Blacky , `` I saw Bowser the other day , or at least some one who look just like him .
Would n't you like to have him back here , Reddy ? ''
`` Most decidedly no , '' reply Reddy with great promptness .
`` A dog be a nuisance .
He be n't of any use in the wide , wide world . ''
`` Not even to drive off Old Man Coyote ? ''
ask Blacky slyly , for he know that more than once Bowser the Hound have help Reddy out of trouble with Old Man Coyote .
Reddy pretend not to hear this .
`` I do n't believe you saw Bowser , '' say he .
`` I do n't believe anybody will ever see Bowser again .
I hope not , anyway . ''
And Blacky knew by the way Reddy say this that it would be quite useless to ask Reddy to help get Bowser home .
CHAPTER XXVII THE ARTFULNESS OF BLACKY Who run in circle never get far .
Bowser the Hound .
To be artful be to be very clever .
It be to do thing in a way so clever that people will not see what you be really do .
No one can be more artful than Blacky the Crow when he set out to be .
Blacky be smart enough not to let Reddy know that he be seek Reddy 's help for Bowser .

He change the subject very abruptly .
`` How be the chicken at Farmer Brown 's ? ''
inquire he .
Reddy look up and grin .
`` They seem to be in just a good health a ever , '' say he , `` so far a I can judge .

He lock them up at night so tight that not even Shadow the Weasel could get his nose inside that henhouse . ''
Blacky 's eye twinkle , but he take care that Reddy should not see them .
`` Farmer Brown 's boy be different from some folk I know , '' say he .
`` How 's that ? ''
demand Reddy Fox .
`` Why , '' reply Blacky , `` there be a certain farmyard I know of where the hen be not keep shut up at all in the daytime , but run around where they please .
I see them every day when I be fly over .
They certainly be fine-looking hen .
I do n't think I 've ever see fatter one .
Some of them be so fat they can hardly run . ''
As Reddy Fox listen , a look of eagerness crept into his eye , and his mouth begin to water .
He just could n't help it .
`` Where do you say those hen be ? ''
he ask , try to speak carelessly .

`` It be a long way from here , Reddy , so I do n't believe you would really be interested . ''

`` I would go a long way if it be worth while .
I do n't suppose you notice if there be any dog about where those hen be ? ''
Blacky pretend not to hear this .
`` I 've often think , '' say he , `` of you and Mrs. Reddy a I have look down at those fat hen .

CHAPTER XXVIII REDDY FOX DREAMS OF CHICKENS It 's a poor watch-dog who sleep with both eye close .
Bowser the Hound .
Reddy Fox watch Blacky the Crow grow small and small until he be just a black speck in the distance .
Finally he disappear .
Reddy look very thoughtful .
He look that way because he be thoughtful .
In fact , Reddy be do a lot of hard thinking .
He be think about those chicken Blacky have tell him of .
The more he think of them , the hungrier he grow .
You see , Reddy have be have rather a hard time to get enough to eat .
`` Yes , Sir , '' say Reddy to himself , `` I would go a long , long distance to get a good plump hen .
I wish I know just where that farm be that that black rascal talk about .
I wonder if he have go that way now .
If I be sure that he have , I would make a little journey in that direction myself .
But I 'm not sure .
That black rascal fly all over the country .
That farm may lie in the direction he have go now , and it may be in quite the opposite direction .
Somehow I 've get to find out in just which direction it be . ''
Reddy yawn , for he have be out all night , and he be sleepy .
He decide that the best thing he could do would be to get a good rest .
One must always be fit if one be to get on in this life .
The hard one must work , the more fit one should keep , and a proper amount of sleep be one of the most necessary thing in keep fit .
So Reddy curl up to sleep .
Hardly have his eye close when he begin to dream .
You see , he have be think so hard about those fat hen , and he be so hungry for one of them , that right away he begin to dream of fat hen .
It be a beautiful dream .
At least , it be a beautiful dream to Reddy .
Fat hen be all about him .
They be so fat that they could hardly walk .
Not only be they fat , but they seem to think that their one object in life be to fill the stomach of hungry fox , for they just stand about wait to be catch .
Never in all his life have Reddy Fox know anything so wonderful a be that dream .
There be no dog to worry him .
There be no hunter with dreadful gun .
All he have to do be to reach out and help himself to a many fat hen a he want .
He ate and ate and ate , all in his dream , you know , and when he could eat no more he start for home .
When he start for home the fat hen that be leave start along with him .
He lead a procession of fat hen straight over to his home in the Old Pasture .
Just imagine how Reddy felt when at last he awake and there be not so much a a feather from a fat hen anywhere about , while his stomach fairly ache with emptiness .
CHAPTER XXIX REDDY TRIES TO AROUSE BLACKY 'S PITY Trust a Fox only as far a you can see him , and lock the chicken up before you do that .
Bowser the Hound .
All the next night , a Reddy Fox hunt and hunt for something to eat , he keep thinking of that dream of fat hen , and he keep wonder how he could get Blacky the Crow to tell him just where that farm with fat hen be .

Reddy be n't fool him a bit .
